рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

тАШрд░рдердВ рдпрд╛рдиреНрддрдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪрддреБрд░реНрджрд╢рд░реНрдЪрдореЗрдХрд╛рджрд╢рдВ рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдХрд╛рдХреНрд╖реАрд╡рддреНрдпрд╛ рдШреЛрд╖рд╛рдпрд╛ рдЖрд░реНрд╖рдВ рдЬрд╛рдЧрддрдорд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирдореН ред тАШрд░рдердВ рдпрд╛рдиреНрддрдореН ’ рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдореН ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд░рдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╢рд╕реНрддреНрд░рдпреЛрд░реБрдХреНрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрдГ рее

Jamison Brereton

40 (866)
As╠Бvins
Ghoс╣г─Б K─Бkс╣г─лvat─л
14 verses: jagat─л
As suggested in the introduction to X.39, we two translators have different interpretations of the ritual context for this pair of hymns. Accordingly we have contributed contrastive, signed discussions of the hymnтАЩs context in this introduction.
SWJ
As already noted, the hymn begins with a mention of the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ chariot journey (vs. 1) and indeed continues with speculations on their whereabouts (vss. 2тАУ3) and a description of our attempts to attract them to our sacrifice (vs. 4). These verses contain vivid imagery, especially the contrastive pictures of sexual pairing in verses 2тАУ3 (see also X.39.14c, which is a mirror image of 40.2d).
These erotic images prepare the way for the scenes of apparent betrothal and marriage that follow (vss. 5тАУ11). These verses open with the speech of a woman identified as Ghoс╣г─Б, whose status as kingтАЩs daughter contrasts with that of the bereft, unnamed woman who speaks in X.39.5 (see the introduction to that hymn). Ghoс╣г─Б boldly addresses the A┼Ыvins themselves and demands to know if they will тАЬbe thereтАЭ for her (vs. 5). The scene sketched is, in my opinion, a Svayaс╣Гvara or womanтАЩs тАЬself-choiceтАЭ marriage. The stage has been set for this in verse 3d, where the A┼Ыvins are described as coming to soma-pressings тАЬlike kingsтАЩ sonsтАЭ (r─Бjaputr─Б╠Б).

This tatpuruс╣гa compound is found only here in the R╠еgveda and would neatly iden tify the A┼Ыvins as appropriate suitors coming to a Svayaс╣Гvara, where the woman making the choice would likewise be a kingтАЩs daughter (5b). Her unabashed speech, questioning them about their suitability as husbands and supporters, would be fit ting in a Svayaс╣Гvara context.
The next verses (6тАУ8) seem to depart from the marriage theme, and it is not possible to be certain that they are spoken by Ghoс╣г─Б. I believe they are, however, because the marital theme continues beneath the surface: verses 5тАУ7 contain four somewhat problematic instances of the preverb pa╠Бri тАЬaroundтАЭ (5a, 6a, 6c, 7c), in the same metrical position, but in awkwardly unidiomatic verbal lexemes. The problems they cause for the translator are seen in the somewhat тАЬoffтАЭ English that represents them. This intrusive pa╠Бri is, in our opinion, an insistent reminder of the wedding context, evoking one of the important parts of the wedding ceremony, the circumambulation of the fire, and also evoking the consummation of the marriage, the embrace of the bride, found close to the end of these wedding verses, in 10d тАЬthe wives are to be embraced (pariс╣гvaje╠Б).тАЭ
Ghoс╣г─БтАЩs likely speech ends with verse 8, ostensibly praising the A┼Ыvins for тАЬgiv ing freedom/wide spaceтАЭ to various individuals and opening up an enclosure with all the characteristics of the Vala cave, a deed not usually attributed to the A┼Ыvins. The wide space created and the opening up of the enclosure can (perhaps fancifully) be taken metaphorically here, in this wedding context, for the deflowering of the virgin bride.
The following two verses (9тАУ10) return to the narrator/poet and describe the wedding itself, but develop the theme identified in the previous verse. In the first p─Бda of verse 9 the maiden is bornтАФpresumably born into womanhood, after the тАЬopening upтАЭ just performed. The тАЬlittle ladтАЭ in flight in the same p─Бda may be her bridegroom, or even a pet diminutive for his penis. The next two p─Бdas (9bc), with sprouting plants and flowing rivers, are generally interpreted as expressing natureтАЩs approval of the marriage; in contrast we again consider them metaphorical, express
ing the advent of sexual maturity and sexual awakening. The sprouting sprouts of p─Бda b remind us of the maiden Ap─Бl─БтАЩs prayer that her pubic hair would grow along with the plants in the fields (VIII.91.5тАУ6); the rivers of p─Бda c might either be her first menstrual blood, the blood from her deflowering, or sexual fluids produced by arousal. This verse ends with the same phrase that Ghoс╣г─Б used in her question to the A┼Ыvins, тАЬbe there for the day,тАЭ but with a reversal of genders (the bride will be there for her husband, as Ghoс╣г─Б asked the A┼Ыvins to be there for her), followed by the triumphant тАЬthis is marriage!тАЭ While verse 9 treats marriage as an intimate exchange between the two principals, verse 10 brings us back to the social aspects of marriage: the exchange relation created between the families and the effort required to bring it about. The mysteries of sex are, mysteriously, touched on in verse 11.
The hymn ends with three verses (12тАУ14) more conventionally addressed to the A┼Ыvins with requests for goods and aid, though the final verse (14) echoes the ques tions about the whereabouts of the A┼Ыvins that began the hymn. JPB
An alternate view of the ritual context of X.39тАУ40 is that both hymns find a place in an Atir─Бtra, an Overnight Soma Sacrifice, in the morning rites that conclude the ceremony. In these rites, which are a continuation of the rites of the Third Pressing from the previous evening, the A┼Ыvins return in the morning of the second day to receive a last offering of soma. The references to the night between evening and morning oblations (e.g., X.40.2), to the soma offerings (X.39.4, 40.13, 14), and, of course, to the A┼Ыvins, to whom both hymns are dedicated, accord with the ritual context of an Atrir─Бtra.
One of the themes of the Third Pressing in the classical soma rites is the fertil ity of the sacrificing couple. Since this is a relatively late hymn, the Wife of the Sacrificer may already have been a participant in the rite for which these hymns were composed. Therefore, the hymns might have been an appeal to the A┼Ыvins to help make the marriage of the sacrificing couple a success by giving them a son. Thus, the тАЬlittle ladтАЭ who тАЬhas taken flightтАЭ in the puzzling verse 9 might be the hoped-for child, whose birth marks the success of their marriage. His тАЬflightтАЭ can refer to his conception; the image of an embryo тАЬflyingтАЭ to the womb also occurs in X.162.3. For a detailed study of the hymn that reflects this interpretation, see Brereton 2013.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhat (worshipper), O leaderes of rites, and where (abiding) glorifies for his good, by his praise at therite, your radiant moving chariot, going (to the sacrifice) at dawn, all-pervading, and bearing (wealth) day afterday to one man after another?тАЭ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWhere are you, A┼Ыvins, by night? Where are you by day? Where do you sojourn? Where do youdwell? Who brings you into his presence in the same plural ce (of sacrifice) as on her couch a widow (brings) herhusband’s brother, as a woman (brings) her husband (to her).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Where in the evening, where at dawn will the A┼Ыvins make their evening meal? Where did they spend the night?
Who takes you to bed, like a widow her brother-in-law, or to a
rendezvous like a maiden a dashing youth?

Griffith

Where are ye, Asvins, in the evening, where at morn? Where is your haltingplace, where rest ye for the night?
Who brings you homeward, as the widow bedward draws her husband’s brother, as the bride attracts the groom?

Geldner

Wo sind denn die Asvin am Abend, wo des Morgens, wo halten sie Einkehr, wo haben sie ├╝bernachtet? Wer nimmt euch zu sich ins Bett wie die Witwe den Schwager, wer bringt euch zur Stelle wie die Maid den J├╝ngling?

Grassmann

Wo weilt des Abends, wo des Morgens, Ritter ihr? wo kehrt ihr ein? und wo verweilet ihr zur Nacht? Wer bringt zu Bett euch wie die Witwe ihren Freund und wie die Braut im Schlafgemach den Br├дutigam?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLeaders (of rites), you are glorified at dawn like two ancient (monarchs) by the voice (of the caller)entitled to worship, you go day by day to the dwelling (of the worshipper); of whose (faults) are you thedestroyer? To whose oblations do you go like princes?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Like two ancieс╣Зс╣н..caller: jaraс╣Зau = two kings, old orgreat by sovereignty;

K─Бpay─Б = the song of the bard or herald, who awakens (a great man) at dawn

Jamison Brereton

You awaken early in the morning like a pitiable [?] old couple; at every dawn you, deserving the sacrifice, come to the house.
For whom do you become occulted, or for whom do you descend to his soma-pressings like kingsтАЩ sons, o men?

Griffith

Early ye sing forth praise as with a herald’s voice, and, meet for worship, go each morning to the house.
Whom do ye ever bring to ruin? Unto whose libations come ye, Heroes, like two Sons of Kings?

Geldner

Fr├╝hmorgens erwachet ihr wie zwei Alte aus Angst, jeden Morgen kommet ihr als Opferw├╝rdige ins Haus. F├╝r wen seid ihr unsichtbar oder zu wessen Somaopfer kommet ihr Herren wie zwei Prinzen?

Grassmann

Des Morgens naht im Wagen wie zwei Greise ihr; bei jedem Fr├╝hlicht kommt ihr hehre zu dem Haus; Wess reiche Geber seid ihr und zu wessen Mahl o M├дnner, eilt ihr, wie zwei K├╢nigss├╢hne bin?

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬLike perons hunting two wild elephants, we praise you, A┼Ыvins, with oblations night and day; at all dueseasons, leaders (of rites), (the worshipper) offers you the oblation; do you, who are rulers of the shining (rain),bring food to mankind.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Hunting two wild elephants: hunting two elephants like tigers

Jamison Brereton

Like hunters on the track of wild elephants, we call you down in the evening and at dawn with our oblation.
You two bring refreshment to the man who pours the libation in proper order, you superior men, you lords of beauty.

Griffith

Even as hunters follow two wild elephants, we with oblations call you down at morn and eve.
To folk who pay you offierings at appointed times, Chiefs, Lords of splendour, ye bring food to strengthen them.

Geldner

Euch locken wir wie die J├дger die wilden Elefanten nachts und morgens mit Opfern herbei. Ihr Herren bringet dem Mann, der p├╝nktlich das Opfer begeht, Speisegenu├Я, ihr Gatten der Sch├╢nheit.

Grassmann

Euch locken Abends Morgens wir durch Opfertrank herbei, wie J├дger durch den Ruf das scheue Wild; Dem Menschen, der zu rechter Zeit: euch Trank ergiesst, dem fahrt ihr reiche Labung zu, o Glanzes Herrn.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬAttending upon you, A┼Ыvins, leaders (of rites), I, Ghoс╣г─Б, the daughter of king (Kakс╣г─лvat), speak toyou and request you; be (present at) my (sacrifice) by day, and be (present) by night, be able, (to grant favour) tothe son of my brother, who has horses and a chariot.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Circling around you two, o A┼Ыvins, Ghoс╣г─Б, the daughter of a king, said, тАЬI ask you, o men:
Will you be there for me for the day and be there for the night? Will you exert your abilities (for me, as if) for a steed (to win the prize) of horse and chariot?1444 X.40

Griffith

To you, O Asvins, came the daughter of a King, Ghosa, and said, O Heroes, this I beg of you:
Be near me in the day, he near me in the night: help me to gain a car-borne chieftain rich in steeds.

Grassmann

Umwandernd euch, des K├╢nigs Tochter Ghoscha ich, hab’ ich’s im Herzen, nun zu bitten, Ritter, euch: Bei mir, o M├дnner, seid bei Tage, seid bei Nacht, und helft dem Lenker sammt dem Wagen und dem Ross.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSage A┼Ыvins, stand by your chariot; make it approach (the sacrifice) of the worshipper, as Kutsa(made his chariot approach) men, the fly carries your honey, A┼Ыvins, in its mouth as a woman carries purified(honey).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As Kutsa…men: Kutsa and Indra ride in the same chariot; cf. RV 4.16.11; as a woman: cf. RV 1.119.2

Jamison Brereton

тАЬYou two poets circle around your chariot, o A┼Ыvins; you arrive at the clans of the singer, as Kutsa (arrived at the poet/Kavi U┼Ыan─Б).
The bee holds the honey of you two encircled with her mouth, o A┼Ыvins, as a young woman (holds) a tryst (within her mouth) [=keeps quiet about it].

Griffith

O Asvins, ye are wise: as Kutsa comes to men, bring your car nigh the folk of him who sings your praise.
The bee, O Asvins, bears your honey in her mouth, as the maid carries it purified in her hand.

Geldner

Ihr seid zwei Weise, ihr Asvin fahret euren Wagen umher; ihr kommet wie Kutsa in die H├дuser des S├дngers. Euch, Asvin, vertraute die Biene mit dem Munde den Honig an wie die Maid den Treffort.

Grassmann

Ihr Ritter haltet weise euren Wagen auf, wie Kutsa dringt ihr zu des S├дngers St├дmmen hin; Die Biene trug im Munde euch den Honig zu; o Ritter, wie zum Stelldichein das M├дdchen kommt.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬYou came, A┼Ыvins, to the rescue of Bhujyu, you came to the rescue of Va┼Ыa, you came to ┼Ъi├▒j─Бrato (hear) his desirable (praise); the offerer of oblations besieges your friendship; and I desire happiness throughyour protection.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

┼Ъi├▒j─Бra: cf. RV 8.5.25; ┼Ъi├▒j─Бra was an Atri; A┼Ыvins came to rescue him from a fire-pit

Jamison Brereton

тАЬYou two came to Bhujyu, o A┼Ыvins, you to Va┼Ыa, you to ┼Ъi├▒j─Бra, to U┼Ыan─Б.
The hostile man will circumvent your comradeship, but I find pleasure in your benevolence along with your help.

Griffith

To Bhujyu and to Vasa ye come near with help, O Asvins, to Sinjara and to Usana.
Your worshipper secures your friendship for himself. Through your protection I desire felicity.

Geldner

Ihr Asvin seid ja dem Bhujyu beigesprungen, ihr dem Vasa, ihr dem Sinjara, dem Usanas. Der Geizige soll eure Freundschaft verpassen; durch eure Gnade bitte ich mir eine Gunst aus.

Grassmann

Zu H├╝lfe kamt dem Bhudschju und dem Va├зa ihr, o Ritter, dem ├Зingara und dem U├зana Um eure Freundschaft werbe nun der Spendende; durch Opferlabung strebe ich nach eurer Gunst.

English translation:

тАЬThe bride, A┼Ыvins, has been born, let the husband approach; may the plural nts spring up (for him) afterthe rain; for him may the streams flow as if from a declivity; may he invulnerable have the power of a husbandover her.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The maiden has been born, and the little lad has taken flight. And when sprouts have sprouted according to (the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ) wondrous powers,
the rivers flow for him as if into a valley; (she) is there for him for the day (and for the night): this is marriage!

Griffith

The Woman hath brought forth, the Infant hath appeared, the plants of wondrous beauty straightway have sprung up.
To him the rivers run as down a deep descent, and he this day becomes their master and their lord.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рдпреБрд╡рдереЛрд░рдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рдд рдпреЗ рдирд░рдГ рдкрддрдпреЛ рдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЬреАрд╡рдВ рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореБрджреНрджрд┐рд╢реНрдп рд░реБрджрдиреНрддрд┐ ред рд░реЛрджрдиреЗрдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЬреАрд╡рдирдореЗрд╡рд╛рд╢рд╛рд╕рдд рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рддрд╛ рдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рдЕрдзреНрд╡рд░реЗ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЗ рд╡рд┐ рдордпрдиреНрддреЗ рдирд┐рд╡реЗрд╢рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЪ рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рддрд╛рд╕реБ рджреАрд░реНрдШрд╛рдВ рдорд╣рддреАрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рддрд┐рдВ рднреБрдЬрдпреЛрдГ рдкреНрд░рдмрдиреНрдзрдирдореН рдЕрдиреБ рджреАрдзрд┐рдпреБрдГ рдЕрдиреБрджрдзрддрд┐ ред рдЗрджрдВ рд╡рд╛рдордВ рд╡рдирдиреАрдпрдордкрддреНрдпрдВ рдкрд┐рддреГрднреНрдпрдГ рд╕рдореАрд░рд┐рд░реЗ рд╕рдВрдкреНрд░реЗрд░рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЪред рддреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рдкрддрд┐рднреНрдпрдГ рдЬрдирдпрдГ рдЬрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рд╖реНрд╡рдЬреЗ рдкрд░рд┐рд╖реНрд╡рдЩреНрдЧрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рдордпрдГ рд╕реБрдЦрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрд╡рдиреНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рее рее резреп рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe husbands who weep for the life (of their wives), make them sit down at the sacrifice, hold in a longembrace, (and) send the Pitс╣Ыs this desirable offspring, upon these husbands the wives (bestow) happiness inorder to be embraced.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Weep for the life of their wives: j─лvam rudanti = liс╣н, they weep for the living; i.e., weep forthe lie (of their wives); by their very weeping they desire to (pray for) their wives’ lives

Jamison Brereton

They cry over the living; they make a mutual exchange at the rite. The men [=relatives of the couple] have been devising (the marriage) for a long stretch:
It is a precious thing for the fathers, that they brought (the couple) together; a joy for husbands that their wives are to be embraced.

Griffith

They mourn the living, cry aloud, at sacrifice: the men have set their thoughts upon a distant cast.
A lovely thing for fathers who have gathered here,-a joy to husbands,-are the wives their arms shall clasp

Geldner

Sie beweinen einen Lebenden, sie sind bei dem Opfer fr├╢hlich; die M├дnner sannen ├╝ber die langen Bande nach. Ein Gutes ist es f├╝r die V├дter, die dieses eingerichtet haben, eine Freude f├╝r die Gatten sind die Frauen zur Umarmung.

Grassmann

Sie beweinen den lebenden, gehen hin und her (?) beim Opferfest; die M├дnner sannen der langen Noth nach, sie, welche hier den Ahnen sch├╢ne Gaben gebracht haben, [w├дhrend] die Weiber ihren Gatten Freude [gew├дhren] zur Umarmung.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins, rich in food, lords of water, twin (associates), may your good will devolve (upon us), may thedesires (of our hearts) be attained; you have been my protectors; may we, (being) beloved, attain the habitationof a husband.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your benevolence has come here, you A┼Ыvins whose goods are prize mares. Our desires have held themselves down firmly in our hearts, A┼Ыvins.
You have become the paired herdsmen, the two lords of beauty. Dear to Aryaman, might we reach his porticos.

Griffith

Your favouring grace hath come, ye Lords of ample wealth: Asvins, our longings are stored up within your hearts.
Ye, Lords of splendour, have become our twofold guard: may we as welcome friends reach Aryaman’s abode.

Geldner

Eure Gunst ist eingetroffen, ihr Reichbelohnende; die W├╝nsche sind euch ans Herz gelegt worden. Ihr wurdet ein Sch├╝tzerpaar, ihr Gatten der Sch├╢nheit. Wir m├╢chten als Geliebte in das Haus eines reichen Freiers gelangen.

Grassmann

Zu uns ist, o Gabenreiche, euer Wohlwollen gekommen; in euren Herzen, o A├зvinen, wurzeln unsre W├╝nsche; ihr seid verzwillingte H├╝ter, o Herrn des Glanzes; als willkommene m├╢chten wir zu Arjamans Wohnung gelangen.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬExulting, do you bestow riches, comprehending male progeny, in the house of my husband, on me,who desire to praise you; lords of waters, make the sacred ford good to drink; remove the tree that stands in theroad and the malevolent (enemy).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Reaching exhilaration in the dwelling of Manu, provide wealth along with heroes to the eloquent one.
Make a ford that offers good drink, o lords of beauty. Smash away the post standing in our path, the malevolence.

Griffith

Even so, rejoicing in the dwelling-place of man, give hero sons and riches to the eloquent.
Make a ford, Lords of splendour, where men well may drink: remove the spiteful tree-stump standing in the path.

Geldner

Grassmann

So gebt nun, euch in dem Hause des Menschen freuend dem Liederkundigen Reichthum der mit allen Helden versehen sei; verschafft ihm eine Tr├дnke mit gutem Tranke, o Herrn des Glanzes, und einen Ruheplatz auf dem Wege; den b├╢se gesinnten schlagt hinweg.

English translation:

тАЬA┼Ыvins of goodly aspect, lords of water, in what plural ce, among what people, do you today delight? Whonow detains you? To the house of what sage or of what sacrificer, have you gone?тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Who has held them down? To the house of which inspired poet or sacrificer have they gone?

Griffith

O Asvins, Wonder-Workers, Lords of lustre, where and with what folk do ye delight yourselves to-day?
Who hath detained them with him? Whither are they gone? Unto what sage’s or what worshipper’s abode?

Geldner

Grassmann

Wo und in welchen H├дusern erfreuen sich heute doch die wunderth├дtigen A├зvinen, die Herren des Glanzes? Wer hat sie zur Einkehr gelenkt? in welches S├дngers oder Opferers Haus sind sie gegangen?

Elizarenkova

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рджрд╕реНрд░рд╛ рд╢реБрднрд╕реНрдкрддреА-рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛) рд╣реЗ рджрд░реНрд╢рдиреАрдп рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдкреНрд░рдж рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдд рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА-рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ !рдЗрд╕рд╕рдордп рдХрд╣рд╛рдБ рд░рд╣рддреЗ рд╣реЛ (рдХрддрдорд╛рд╕реБ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реБ рдорд╛рджрдпреЗрддреЗ) рдЖрдк рдХрд┐рди рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рдУрдВ рдореЗрдВ рд╣рд░реНрд╖ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реЛ (рдХрдГ-рдИрдВ рдирд┐рдпреЗрдореЗ) рдХреМрди рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрде рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рди рдкрд░ рд░реЛрдХрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдпрд╛ рдирд┐рдпрдо рд╕реЗ рд░рдЦрддрд╛ рд╣реИред (рдХрддрдорд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рдЬрдЧреНрдорддреБрдГ) рдХрд┐рд╕ рд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡реА рдХреЗ рдпрд╛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рди рдХреЗ рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рд░реНрде рдШрд░ рдХреЛ рдЬрд╛рддреЗ рд╣реЛ, рдЗрд╕ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рд╕рднреА рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА-рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдШрд░ рдирд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд┐рдд рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдХреА рдЖрдХрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд░рдиреА рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдП реерезрекрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдг рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдд рд╡реГрджреНрдз рд╕реНрддреНрд░реА-рдкреБрд░реБрд╖реЛрдВ рдХреЗ рдкрд╛рд╕ рдЬрд╛рдХрд░ рдкреВрдЫрдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдП рдХрд┐ рдЖрдк рдХрд┐рд╕ рдШрд░ рдореЗрдВ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рджреЗрддреЗ рд╣реЛ, рдХрд╣рд╛рдБ рддреБрдо рд╕рддреНрдХрд╛рд░ рдФрд░ рд╣рд░реНрд╖ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рдХрд░рддреЗ рд╣реЛ, рдХреМрди рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрде рдЖрджрд░ рд╕реЗ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдШрд░ рд░рдЦрддрд╛ рд╣реИ ? рдЗрд╕ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдЙрдирд╕реЗ рдкреВрдЫрдХрд░ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рдХ рдмрд░реНрддрд╛рд╡ рдХрд░ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдШрд░ рдмреБрд▓рд╛рдХрд░ рд▓рд╛рдн рдЙрдард╛рдПрдБ реерезрекрее

рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордореБрдирд┐ - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - (рджрд╕реНрд░рд╛ рд╢реБрднрд╕реНрдкрддреА-рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдирд╛) рд╣реЗ рджрд░реНрд╢рдиреАрдпреМ тАЬрджрд╕реН рджрд░реНрд╢рдиреЗтАЭ [рдЪреБрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдГ] рдФрдгрд╛рджрд┐рдХреЛ рд░рдХреН рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ, рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдиреМ рдХрд▓реНрдпрд╛рдгрдкреНрд░рджреМ рд╕реБрд╢рд┐рдХреНрд╖рд┐рддреМ рд╕реНрдерд╡рд┐рд░реМ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖реМ ! рдпреБрд╡рд╛рдореН (рдЕрджреНрдп рдХреНрд╡рд╕реНрд╡рд┐рддреН) рдЕрджреНрдп рдХреБрддреНрд░ рд╣рд┐ рд╕реНрдердГ (рдХрддрдорд╛рд╕реБ рд╡рд┐рдХреНрд╖реБ рдорд╛рджрдпреЗрддреЗ) рдХрддрдорд╛рд╕реБ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛рд╕реБ рд╣рд░реНрд╖рдорд╛рдкреНрдиреБрдердГ (рдХрдГ рдИрдореН-рдирд┐рдпреЗрдореЗ) рдХрдГ рдЦрд▓реБ рдЧреГрд╣рд╕реНрде рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗрд╜рд╡рд░реЛрдзрдпрддрд┐ рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдирд┐рдпрдореЗрди рд░рдХреНрд╖рддрд┐ (рдХрддрдорд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛ рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рдЬрдЧреНрдорддреБрдГ) рдХрддрдорд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖реЛ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдиреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдпрдЬрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рд╕рддреНрдХрд░реНрддреБрдВ рдЧреГрд╣рдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрдердГ-рдЬрдЧреНрдорддреБрдГ рдордзреНрдпрдорд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреЗ рдкреНрд░рдердорд╛ рд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпреЗрди рдПрддреМ-рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд┐рдиреМ рд╕реНрдерд╡рд┐рд░реМ рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╛рд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдЪрд╛рд░рдгрд╛ рд╕реНрд╡рдЧреГрд╣реЗ рдирд┐рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдгрд╛рдХрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╛ реерезрекрее
